TITLE      Prompt-fission-neutron spectra in the 239Pu(n,f)       14684  1    3 
           reaction                                               14684  1    4 
AUTHOR     (P.Marini,J.Taieb,B.Laurent,G.Belier,A.Chatillon,      14684  1    5 
           D.Etasse,P.Morfouace,M.Devlin,J.A.Gomez,R.C.Haight,    14684  1    6 
           K.J.Kelly,J.M.O'Donnell,K.T.Schmitt)                   14684  1    7 
INSTITUTE  (2FR BRC,2FR CAE,1USALAS)                              14684  1    8 
REFERENCE  (J,PR/C,101,044614,2020)                               14684  1    9 
FACILITY   (LINAC,1USALAS) The experiment was carried out at the  14684  1   10 
           WNR facility at Los Alamos National Laboratory.        14684  1   11 
SAMPLE     (94-PU-239,ENR=0.9990) 239Pu was placed inside         14684  1   12 
           fission chamber. Total of 47 mg of 239Pu was arranged  14684  1   13 
           in 22 deposits on every cathode of the fission         14684  1   14 
           chamber. Diameter of each deposit was 33 mm.           14684  1   15 
DETECTOR   (IOCH) Fission fragments are detected in a multilayer  14684  1   16 
           fission chamber containing a stack of axial            14684  1   17 
           ionization cells. 11 cathodes with fissile deposits    14684  1   18 
           are on ground potential. Anode gap was 2.5 mm. The     14684  1   19 
           chamber was filled with CF4 gas to ensure a fast       14684  1   20 
           charge collection and operates 100 mbar above the      14684  1   21 
           local atmospheric pressure. A time resolution better   14684  1   22 
           than 0.8ns full width at half maximum could be         14684  1   23 
           achieved.                                              14684  1   24 
           (SCIN) Prompt fission neutrons were detected using     14684  1   25 
           Chi-Nu high energy neutron detector array. The array   14684  1   26 
           consists of 54 EJ-309 liquid scintillator detectors,   14684  1   27 
           read by photomultipliers, and arranged on a            14684  1   28 
           hemisphere with inner radius of about 1m around the    14684  1   29 
           fission chamber. Diameter of each detector was 17.78   14684  1   30 
           cm and thickness 5.08 cm. The detectors are placed at  14684  1   31 
           nine different angles, with six detectors per angle,   14684  1   32 
           theta(lab) ranging from 30 deg to 150 deg, with        14684  1   33 
           respect to the beam axis. A 2 mm thick Pb shield was   14684  1   34 
           placed in front of each detector to reduce the amount  14684  1   35 
           of low energy gamma rays. Pulse shape discrimination   14684  1   36 
           technique was used to distinguish neutrons and gamma   14684  1   37 
           rays. The whole array covers close to 10% of 4Pi       14684  1   38 
           solid angle.                                           14684  1   39 
METHOD     (TOF) Primary as well as secondary neutron energy was  14684  1   40 
           determined by time of flight. Proton beam consist of   14684  1   41 
           625 mu-s long macropulses with repetition rate of      14684  1   42 
           100 Hz. Each macropulse is composed of series of 250 ps14684  1   43 
           wide micropulses separated by 1.8 mu-s. A 1.27-cm thick14684  1   44 
           polyethylene absorber was placed into the beam line to 14684  1   45 
           harden the spectra and reduce the wraparound effect.   14684  1   46 
           Fission detector was placed at a distance 20 m from    14684  1   47 
           the spallation target.                                 14684  1   48 
INC-SOURCE (SPALL) A white pulsed neutron beam was produced by    14684  1   49 
           spallation of thick tungsten target by 800 MeV pulsed  14684  1   50 
           proton beam.                                           14684  1   51 
ERR-ANALYS (DATA-ERR) Total uncertainties                         14684  1   52
